Disaster Relief is Saving Lives

Donate One More Penny, Save One More Life

Telegram

To Xu Junjian, Director of the Jiangsu Guiding Huai River into the Sea Project: I recently read the Shen Bao of October 3rd, and the Xinwen Bao of the same day, both carrying reports that Engineer Shen Caiyi of the Huai River Project sent a telegram to the office, stating that County Magistrate Deng of Shuyang reported to the office that thousands of pine trees and thousands of bundles of rice straw, more than two thousand sacks and twelve thousand rush bags, and ten tons of lead wire were used for the emergency rescue project, which are all untrue. He also stated that ten tons of lead wire would weigh more than six thousand tons, and assuming each train car carries thirty tons, it would take more than two hundred cars to transport them. Shuyang is a remote county and certainly does not have such a large amount of lead wire. The wood pilings were requisitioned from Donghai County. As for the number of sacks and rush bags, whether the quantity is factual can be inferred. Furthermore, when the new dike breached, the county magistrate did not send a single person to stop the breach. Please investigate, etc. I have read the Xin Hai Bao and Su Bei Daily, which have similar records. I am very surprised. Upon investigation, on the night of September 20th, at the central opening of the old Six Tang River dike, I was personally at the construction site. At that time, due to the high water pressure and difficulty in obtaining earth, it was impossible to stop the breach. I telegraphed to dispatch hundreds of laborers from Yangkou, using tree pilings and door panels to protect the place where the breach of the old dike led directly to the new dike, and sent a Huang Protection Committee member Wang Shirong to escort four sailing boats from Tanggou, which were arranged in the above-mentioned place to block the water flow. After the emergency protection was in place, they went to Tanggou, on the one hand dispatching laborers from Tanggou to the new dike to drive piles and add firewood, and on the other hand discussing with the two county magistrates He and Xu, and the three counties jointly carried out the emergency protection of the new dike. Muyang sent five thousand laborers, Donghai three thousand, Siyang one thousand five hundred. The laborers from Muyang who should have been sent could not be conscripted because the west of the river had already been flooded. The water level of Nan Liu Tang was not yet flat, and there was no danger, so three thousand five hundred laborers were telegraphed from the five townships of Gao Dong, Gao Xi, Gao Nan, Gao Bei, Shuohu and the two towns of Yangkou and Gaogou, and eight hundred people each were dispatched from the fifth and eighth districts. The laborers from Yangkou and Gaogou towns immediately crossed the river to the new dike opposite Yangkou, and the laborers from the fifth district had also approached Tanggou. I, together with the two county magistrates He and Xu, and the three engineers Shen, Wang and Xue, went to the new dike to inspect. Before half of the journey was completed, it was reported that there was a breach in front, so we turned around and retreated, and the back road also breached. We went under the dike to bypass the water head, then went to the top of the dike, and another place in front of our feet breached. After desperately jumping over it, another place at the rear breached. The dike body was near the water for only four hours, and the water level was no more than two Luo Chi at the deepest point. Within five minutes, there were four breaches, and the quality of the dike was as fragile as rice flour, and when it encountered water, it was like boiling water. At that time, everyone who saw it thought that the entire dike would collapse, but I thought it could not be rescued, and even the engineers thought there was no way. After discussion at the Tanggou Township Office, I and County Magistrate He immediately retreated to the north bank of the Chaimi River. County Magistrate Xu returned to protect the Yan River. The above-mentioned course of events can be described in detail not only by the two county magistrates He and Xu, but also by the two engineers Yuan and. Shen Caiyi returned to the dangerous place, knowing the truth, but deliberately set up words to attack Xu, and did not know what his intention was. As for the Donghai people, they assisted in repairing the Chaimi North Dike, and did not bring pile grass. It was all supplied by Shuyang. As for the West Dike of the Liu Tang River, only four hundred more people were dispatched by me from Donghai on the afternoon of September 20th to repair the Heng Dike above Tanggou. All the pile grass was taken on the spot. The willows along the banks of the Liu Tang and Chaimi Rivers were almost completely cut down. The willow stakes used in Moyang, and the number claimed by the engineer, will be ten times more than this. The number of rice straw is even more than this. The above-mentioned willow stakes are all requisitioned on the spot and not valued. The public can see and hear this, and no one dares to fabricate the price to profit, so there is no need to argue. The rush bags and sacks used have not yet been settled. The reports from various parts have not been received. I can't figure it out for a while. As for what the official said, Shuyang reported that ten tons of lead wire had been used, and added fuel to the fire to frighten people. I don't know which month and day of the report the official based on in this county. How much has the county applied for the expenses for flood control before and after, and the Jun office has accounts to check, and no money has been taken from the local area. How can there be financial resources to buy so many tons of lead wire? This government has not made such a false report, and the official deliberately fabricated the facts and tarnished the reputation, which is not worth a smile to the knowledgeable. However, the talk of the city tiger, the hearers change color, Zeng Shen killed people, and his mother was also shocked. Xianghai has been serving as an official in Shanghai for nearly twenty years. He has no other strengths, but he can be confident in his integrity. The official's unfounded slander is regarded as a lifelong shame and humiliation. Reputation is the second life, and it is difficult to remain silent. I have to declare the facts and respectfully ask you to approve, and send letters to various newspapers to correct them. I am very grateful. Deng Xianghai, County Magistrate of Shuyang, kowtows.

Now the two industry associations have notified their member banks and money shops to comply. Xin Sheng She reporters learned from the banking industry yesterday that the long-term credit loans are divided into two periods each year, the end of April and the end of October. The business of money shops focuses on credit loans. The total amount of loans due at the end of October this year is more than 50 million yuan. The loans extended by Ningbo money shops in Shanghai are about 15 million yuan. The business of banks focuses on mortgage loans. As for long-term credit loans, the amount is very small. Industrial and commercial circles that have borrowed money have been in contact with money shops and banks in recent days to settle interest, extend the loans, or make new loans or repay them. However, the settlement of interest and extension of loans are the main focus.

Now this investigation is scheduled to end today, and no more persuasion will be given. The City Council Sends a Letter to the Public Works Department Requesting Prudent Handling of Telephone Rate Increases, Which Should Consider the Interests of Citizens to Avoid Further Troubles

The Takung Society reports that the Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Association, regarding the issue of telephone rate increases by the Shanghai Telephone Company, after the Public Works Department of the Public Concession hired telephone experts from China, Britain, America, and Japan to come to Shanghai and participate in the Telephone Expert Committee for research, has already completed its work and is now compiling a final report to be submitted to the Public Works Department for adoption. However, according to reports in various newspapers, the British, American, and Japanese experts still advocate charging by call. This news has spread, causing public consternation. The association convened its second representative meeting and resolved to firmly oppose telephone rate increases and charging by call. If necessary, it will also convene a user meeting to discuss countermeasures. Yesterday, it sent a letter to the Public Works Department, requesting prudent handling of telephone rate increases and charging issues to avoid disputes. The original letter stated: "Respectfully, regarding the issue of telephone rate increases by the Shanghai Telephone Company, your department hired experts from China, America, Britain, and Japan to come to Shanghai for research, and a final report has been compiled and submitted to your department for consideration. According to reports, the Expert Committee still advocates charging by call. Upon hearing this, the public is alarmed. We believe that telephone service is a public utility, and its function is to facilitate communication. The level of charges should be based on the economic capacity of the citizens, as has been repeatedly communicated in previous letters. Moreover, at a time when the local economy is in panic and worsening, and the southern industries are in decline day by day, people are already feeling severe pressure from existing expenses and are unable to maintain them. How can they bear any further burdens? Regarding telephone charges, if charging by call and disguised rate increases are adopted, users will find it impossible to endure and will have no choice but to jointly dismantle their telephones. We believe that telephones are of great importance to social stability. If they are jointly dismantled, the company will not benefit, and the stability of the concession will be greatly affected. Your council, as the highest authority for managing the administrative and security affairs of the concession, should take into account the interests of the tax-paying citizens and give careful consideration and strict handling to the issue of telephone rate increases and charging by call, so as to avoid further troubles. This would be fortunate for society and fortunate for the citizens. Respectfully addressed to the Public Works Department of the Public Concession."

The Second Special District Citizens' Association has previously expressed its opposition to telephone rate increases. Now, the company is about to change its charging method to charging by call. If this method is implemented, telephone bills will inevitably increase immediately. In order to prevent the company from charging by call and ease the burden on users, the association sent a letter to the Public Works Department yesterday, requesting them to find ways to prevent this. The original letter is recorded as follows: "Respectfully, in recent times, the market has been sluggish, all industries are declining, and the economy is stagnant, reaching a critical point. At this time, all public utilities should reduce their prices to jointly maintain the precarious situation. However, the telephone company fails to see this and repeatedly raises prices despite the extreme economic panic of the citizens. Recently, we heard that they are about to change the charging method to charging by call. If this method is implemented, telephone bills will inevitably exceed the original amount by several times, and the burden on users will increase immediately. Since telephone service is a public utility, the telephone charges cannot be calculated solely for the benefit of the company without considering the burden on users. The company's insistence on going its own way not only violates the principle of public utilities but also disrupts social order and peace of mind. If swift measures are not taken to prevent this, what will become of the users? This association, witnessing the collapse of the market, deeply wishes not to see the phenomenon of social unrest again. Therefore, we are writing to earnestly request your department to consider the difficulties of business and quickly forward a letter to the company, urging them not to implement the method of charging by call, in order to comply with public sentiment and ease the burden on users. This would be greatly appreciated. Respectfully addressed to the Public Works Department of the French Concession."

Hong San Telephones Shanghai to Report on Disaster Conditions in Xihua and Other Counties; Xihua County Has 550,000 Mu of Flooded Farmland; Disaster Situation in Shangshui is Similar to That in Xihua

The Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Flood Relief in Various Provinces recently received a telegram from Hong San, Director of the Henan Disaster Relief Office, reporting on the disaster situation in the Xihua County area. The original telegram is as follows:

Disaster Relief Telegram

Chairman and Gentlemen,

Your instructions have been respectfully received. Since returning from Fengqiu, San and two staff members went south to Xihua this month. The next day, together with the county magistrate and others, we personally inspected the disaster area and the breach in the Shahe River at Nandukou. The county has over 550,000 mu of flooded farmland, and over 4,900 houses have been washed away. The number of affected households is as high as over 40,000. The situation is dire and unbearable to witness, especially in Zhuchumu and Yangsizhuang in the Sixth District. Located on the banks of the Shahe River, they bear the brunt of the breach. The water has been flooded for three months, and no crops remain. Although the floodwaters have receded, the land is covered with sand and is no longer suitable for cultivation. Many residents live in grass huts, barely surviving. Their state of starvation is truly heartbreaking. When we arrived near Zhuzhuang, hundreds of elderly women, carrying infants in their arms, knelt on the road, tears streaming down their faces, begging for prompt relief. After much consolation, they dispersed. Their eagerness to survive is evident. We continued south and arrived in Dengcheng in the Fifth District of Shangshui County. Guided by Zhang, the section chief representing the county, we inspected the second, third, and fourth disaster areas. The water from the breach in the Shahe River inundated these areas, so the disaster area covers almost the entire county. The autumn harvest is hopeless, many livestock have died, and the residents are emaciated, barely surviving. The situation is as dire as in Xihua. We returned to Kaifeng and made a brief stay. The office has now been surveyed and determined to be located in the disaster-affected children's orphanage along the Hebei River in Zhengzhou. As for the date of distribution, as soon as the relief tickets arrive, we will send personnel to various counties to begin household surveys and distribution.

Hong San of the Henan Disaster Relief Office of the Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Flood Relief in Various Provinces kowtows.

Assistance from All Sides

All directors and staff of the local Chinese Merchant Electric Tram Company, out of sympathy for the compatriots in the disaster areas of various provinces, donated several thousand yuan from the company's directors and staff. In addition, the company's entire tram operating revenue for the Double Tenth Festival was used to raise a total of 10,000 yuan for relief. Yesterday, the company sent a letter with the donation to the Disaster Relief Committee for distribution in the disaster areas. In addition, the Jiashan County Disaster Relief Fundraising Opera Performance Office also remitted over 189 yuan to the relief fund yesterday through the Bank of China.

Seafarer Examinations Extended to Mid-December; One Month Extension; Order to Seafarers to Take Examinations Promptly

The Ministry of Communications is conducting seafarer examinations. Those who have not been examined have been ordered by the Ministry to the Maritime Affairs Bureaus in Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, and other ports to begin conducting examinations for both deck and engine department seafarers from the 16th of this month for a period of one month, ending on November 14th. Seafarers who have not been examined have been ordered to register and take the examinations promptly, otherwise their seafarer service qualifications will be revoked. Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua sent a telegram to Shanghai yesterday, stating that the seafarer examinations have been scheduled to end on November 14th. However, considering that there are over 1,000 merchant ships nationwide, requiring a large number of seafarers, the registration and examination dates are now extended from November 20th to December 15th. This one-month extension is to provide an opportunity for seafarers who have not yet taken the examinations to take them. If they do not take the examinations by this deadline, it will be difficult to make up the examinations. A special telegram has been sent to the local shipping companies to inform all seafarers to comply.

The Social Affairs Bureau Actively Plans and Strictly Organizes the National Products Market; New Registration Rules Promulgated; Those Who Violate Them Will Be Banned

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau considers that there are many temporary national products markets and national products exhibitions recently established in this city. However, the more there are, the easier it is for them to become abusive. Some of them may have unsound organizations, which will not only fail to fulfill the responsibility of promoting national products but also affect the reputable temporary national products markets and national products exhibitions. This will inevitably be more harmful than beneficial. In order to prevent the establishment of such unsoundly organized national products markets and to ensure the sound organization of various markets, the Social Affairs Bureau has recently formulated and officially promulgated the "Registration Rules for National Products Markets and National Products Exhibitions in This City." The rules stipulate that those who apply to hold a temporary national products market or a national products exhibition must submit the articles of association one month in advance, stating the location of the venue, its layout, the types of manufacturers and products participating, and other details. The application must be signed by all the organizers and submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for registration. Temporary markets or exhibitions approved by the Social Affairs Bureau must still comply with the regulations of the relevant competent authorities regarding construction, sanitation, water and electricity, traffic safety, and fire protection. Those who violate the provisions of the registration rules or change their content after being approved for registration will be banned by the Social Affairs Bureau. The full text of the rules is recorded below:

Article 1: Those who hold or solicit manufacturers in this city to hold a temporary national products market or a national products exhibition in other cities must comply with the provisions of these rules.

Article 2: Temporary national products markets or national products exhibitions, except those organized by the competent authorities, may be initiated by established commercial organizations or by 50 or more national products manufacturers with real capital.

Article 3: Those who apply to hold a temporary national products market or a national products exhibition must submit the articles of association one month in advance, stating the following details. The application must be signed by all the organizers and submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for registration: (1) Location of the venue and its layout (with drawings); (2) Duration of the exhibition and the date of preparation; (3) Participating manufacturers and types of products; (4) Estimated income and expenditure.

Article 4: The applicant shall, within five days after the registration is approved, submit a list of the names, addresses, and resumes of the members of the preparatory committee and the persons in charge of the conference, together with a statement of the production methods and supporting documents, to the Social Affairs Bureau for record.

Article 5: The applicant shall prepare for and hold the event within the time limit after the registration is approved. If the event is postponed for any reason, the applicant shall submit a written explanation to the Social Affairs Bureau for approval before the deadline.

Article 6: After approving the registration, the Social Affairs Bureau shall notify the relevant agencies and organizations to provide assistance.

Article 7: When preparing to hold a temporary national products market or a national products exhibition, the preparatory expenses shall be borne equally by the organizers.

Article 8: The account books and vouchers shall be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for review.

Article 9: Those who violate the provisions of these rules or change their content after being approved for registration will be banned by the Social Affairs Bureau.

Article 10: Temporary markets or exhibitions approved by the Social Affairs Bureau must still comply with the regulations of the relevant competent authorities regarding construction, sanitation, water and electricity, traffic safety, security, and fire protection.

Article 11: If there are any matters not covered in these rules, they may be amended at any time.

Article 12: These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Shanghai Municipal Government.

Overseas Chinese Zhang Yongqin Brings His Wife to Shanghai; Forced to Return to Japan by the Japanese Consulate; Arrested at the Lao Gongxin Hotel in Shiliupu; Couple Inevitably Separated After Interrogation

The Shiye Society reports that overseas Chinese Zhang Yongqin, a native of Yongjia County, Zhejiang Province, has been running a noodle shop in Chiba Prefecture, Japan, for many years. He married a Japanese woman from that area as his wife. They worked hard all day and were able to make a decent living. Recently, he was forced to close his business by the police station in the county, leaving him unable to stand on his feet. He went alone to Nagasaki to wait for a ship to return to China. His wife found out about this, and determined not to serve two husbands, she hoped to share the joys and sorrows. With the consent of her parents, she pursued him to Nagasaki and boarded a ship of the Da Lai Company with her husband, arriving in Shanghai on the 11th. Unexpectedly, as soon as they arrived at the Lao Gongxin Hotel, the Japanese Consulate sent personnel with documents, accompanied by the Shiliupu Public Security Branch, to arrest Zhang Yongqin and his wife and take them back to the consulate for interrogation. As a result, Zhang Yongqin was forced to send his wife back to Japan. Unable to do otherwise, Mr. Zhang accompanied his wife on the Shanghai Maru today and left Shanghai to return to Japan. The situation was very tragic.

The Municipal Zoo Releases Statistics on Park Visits for Last Month; A Total of 72,201 People; An Increase of Over 22,000 People Compared to August

The Municipal Zoo on Wenmiao Road had a total of 72,201 visitors in September, an increase of 16,648 people compared to August. This included 60,452 adults, 11,490 children, soldiers, and police, and 6259 people in groups, totaling 72,201 people.

In addition, since the opening of the whale exhibition hall in the park on the 1st of this month, there has been an unusually large number of visitors to the park. As of yesterday, the total number of visitors was 48,344. On the Double Tenth Festival alone, there were 10,826 visitors. On the other days, there were over 4,000 visitors each day.

Young Woman Sues Husband for Cohabitation

Li Shi Xiuying, a young woman from Ningbo, recently hired lawyer Hu Yuanjun to sue her husband, Li Bingnan, in the local court for abandonment, demanding cohabitation and the return of 4,000 yuan in living expenses and 300 yuan in education expenses for her son. The facts are as follows: The plaintiff married at the age of 20. The defendant is the manager and director of a bookstore, and also holds important positions such as accounting department and lease account room of Shanghai __ Nursing Home, with considerable income. He secretly kept a mistress outside. Last autumn, the plaintiff discovered this and tried to persuade him. The defendant knew he was wrong and wrote a letter of repentance, which he gave to the plaintiff to keep, guaranteeing that the same incident would not happen again. However, last winter, the defendant again had a secret rendezvous with a woman in Room 26 of the Wuzhou Hotel. The plaintiff caught them in person. Afterwards, he repeatedly refused to correct his behavior. Since February of this year, he has not paid household expenses (30 yuan per month) and pocket money (10 yuan per month), totaling 280 yuan for seven months. He often stayed out all night. On April 23rd, he ran away, and there was no news of him. On the 27th, the plaintiff posted a notice in the newspaper to look for him. On May 30th, the defendant led a group of people to force the plaintiff to the Xin Xin Hotel to sign and fingerprint a divorce agreement that they had written. The plaintiff played along and instructed the defendant to sign and fingerprint first. At this point, the plaintiff could no longer bear it and shouted for help. The plaintiff saw that they were panicked and fled. The plaintiff only knew to be faithful to one man until the end. Therefore, she requested that the defendant be summoned to court and ordered to cohabitate, and to allocate living expenses. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Chen summoned the parties for questioning. The woman testified about the previous events and requested legal aid. It was decided to wait for investigation and then conduct a joint trial.

Opium and Gambling Den Raided at the Juelu Hotel; 14 People Arrested; To Be Handed Over to the Court Today

A detective from the Public Concession Lao Zha Station received a report that there was an opium and gambling den in Room 108 on the second floor of the Juelu Hotel on Xizang Road. He immediately sent Chinese and Western detectives, and escorted the informant to the room for identification. At that time, the gamblers were playing mahjong and the opium addicts were lying on their beds, smoking opium. The detectives immediately carried out the arrest. The owner, Chen Akun, and 14 gamblers and opium addicts, including Ji Zhengshou (nicknamed "Small Market Cake"), Zhang Juquan, and Fan Achun, were arrested on the spot. Four opium pipes, eight opium lamps, and the equipment for storing opium (a mechanism installed under the seat) and gambling tools were seized and taken to the police station for interrogation. It is reported that the gambling den had large winnings and losses, and the daily commission was several hundred yuan. They will be handed over to the court this morning for trial.

Kidnapper Ren Chan Hong Detained for Further Questioning; Still Another Unresolved Kidnapping Case

On the 9th of this month, at noon, Lu Xiufeng, the five-year-old daughter of Lu Kunquan, a native of Changzhou living at No. 760 Taopeng Road, suddenly disappeared while playing at the doorstep. Lu searched everywhere but could not find her. He was informed by his fellow villager, Ren Chan Hong, that she had been abducted to the home of his friend Zhang Ronghai at No. 52 Tokyo Road. Ren falsely claimed that Xiufeng was his niece and that she was temporarily staying there overnight because her brother and sister-in-law were quarreling and no one was taking care of her, and that he would come to pick her up the next day. He also asked someone to try to sell the girl for money. Zhang believed him and readily agreed. Later, Tao Jiankang, a native of Anhui who runs a pancake shop next door, reported to Lu that his daughter had been abducted by Ren Chan Hong and that he could find out by asking him. Lu knew Ren, so he went to his home at No. 15 Yangshupu Road to look for his daughter, but he could not find her. When he questioned Ren about where she was hidden, Ren initially denied it. The Chinese detectives Peng Zhenxuan and Liu Zhisheng arrived and arrested Ren. Ren then revealed where Xiufeng was hidden. They rushed to Zhang Ronghai's place, found Lu's daughter, and returned her to her father. The suspect, Ren, was taken to the Yulin Road police station for detention. Yesterday, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The Public Works Department lawyer, ___ Zhishan, described the events and stated that there was still another kidnapping case involving the defendant that had not been clarified, and requested a postponement. Subsequently, the victim, Lu Kunquan, and witnesses Zhang Ronghai and Tao Jiankang, explained what had happened. They questioned the defendant, whose testimony was evasive. Judge ___ Lu Fen ordered him to be returned to custody and scheduled another hearing.

Mei Lanfang Advocates for Disaster Victims; Speaks on Performing to Aid Relief

Central News Agency reports: Since the beginning of summer this year, the Yangtze and Yellow River basins have experienced successive floods, inundating fields and homes, and causing people and livestock to be swept away. The disaster is extremely severe, affecting more than ten provinces and millions of people. Relief efforts are urgently needed. Therefore, various sectors of this city, responding to the needs of the situation, have specially initiated and established the Provincial Flood Relief Associations to advocate for the disaster victims. Since the commencement of work, the amount of support from all parties and enthusiastic donations of money and goods from people of all walks of life has been substantial. In addition to the charity performances previously held at the New World and the film star aid concert at the Great Shanghai Garden, Mr. Mei Lanfang, who recently arrived in the country, has been invited to perform at the Golden Theater to aid relief. The grand scenes of the past few days have been repeatedly recorded in newspapers. Yesterday, reporters specially visited Mr. Mei Lanfang and Mr. Li Dachao, deputy director of the fundraising group of the Flood Relief Association, to inquire about everything. Details are specially recorded below:

Mr. Mei's Remarks

Reporters noted that Mr. Mei's willingness to perform despite his illness to advocate for disaster victims demonstrates a commendable public-spirited enthusiasm. Therefore, we specially visited Mr. Mei the day before yesterday. He first stated that he received much support from various parties before going abroad. Upon returning to the country, he was further encouraged by various sectors. Such gratitude and pleasant emotions cannot be described in words. He can only work hard to live up to the expectations of the people. As for the issues of improving national opera and Western opera, learning from each other's strengths, and compensating for weaknesses, he has already briefly reported upon his return to the country, which has been published in newspapers. No need to elaborate further. However, this mission involves great responsibility, and cannot be accomplished by an individual alone. He hopes that writers and playwrights can offer guidance and assistance. Currently, what he can do is only start from small things. However, each has its own strengths, such as the time-saving and economic aspects of national opera, the dance steps, and so on, which others cannot match. When he visited Europe previously, he watched various dramas more than seventy times. Although he dares not say he has a deep understanding, the impressions he gained of the essence of various dramas are quite profound. Therefore, he is eager to make improvements to the best of his ability. The stones from other hills can be used to polish jade. After returning to the country, he originally intended to rest temporarily. While recuperating, he would take this opportunity to conduct diligent and focused research on national opera. However, the disaster situation in various places this year is severe, unseen in a century. As a citizen, he should have sympathy and compassion, and should do his best. After completing performances in Beijing and Hangzhou, he returned to Shanghai and, urged by various parties, he reluctantly contributed his meager efforts. He is deeply encouraged by the care and expectations of all parties.

Mr. Li's Remarks

The Flood Relief Association was established in August this year by more than one hundred leaders of various groups and organizations in this city. Yesterday, reporters visited Mr. Li Dachao, deputy director of the fundraising group of the association. He said that when the association was established, he contributed several fundraising plans, which were passed by the general meeting and assigned to different groups to implement. These included general donations, donations from the wealthy, city-wide rent donations, the city's film industry, the dance industry, and designating one day's operating income to be fully used for relief. These have been gradually implemented. In addition to fundraising through various channels, a charity fair was held at the New World and a "Hundred Flowers Aid Relief" concert was held last month, as well as a film star aid relief concert at the Great Shanghai Garden. There were also national martial arts aid relief competitions, football aid relief competitions, swimming aid relief competitions, and so on. Each event achieved excellent results and had a significant impact. He hopes that gentlemen, ladies, and celebrities will provide enthusiastic support to save the people affected by the disaster.

Donations from Various Parties

The association continued to receive donations in the past two days, including 309.24 yuan from the Shanghai Citizen-Run Wireless Broadcasting Industry Association through Yongshun Bank's Zhou Fusheng Chuan and 32 households; 230 yuan from Mr. Nie Hanzhang through Huiyun Layman's Hongde Yu Paper Shop and 7 colleagues; 235.19 yuan from 13 households including Lin Huaisang and Lin Huguang, employees of the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum Administration; 176 yuan from 21 households including Song Wanfu and Tao Sheng collected by Fuyuan Zhuang; 1318.4 yuan from 13 households including the Shanghai All Circles Establish Chiang Kai-shek Memorial Hall Preparatory Committee; 1008.28 yuan collected by Jin Cheng Bank on behalf of Weitong Heji Yarn Factory; 1900.21 yuan collected by Shen Bao on behalf of Li Sheng and 94 households; and 10 yuan from Mr. Lin Kanghou's charity auction donation to Liu Baisheng.

Rue Massenet: Private Counterfeiting Operation Cracked; Over 700 Forged Lead Coins Seized; Woman, Wang Ding, and Gu Zhusheng Arrested

Detectives Lü Zhulin and Cai Jinzhang of the French Concession Police learned on the 10th of this month that a private lead coin counterfeiting operation was being secretly conducted at No. 374 Rue Massenet. These coins were being mixed into circulation, disrupting the financial system, and violating criminal law. They immediately led officers to No. 374 Rue Massenet at 10:00 AM on the same day. They arrested Wang Ding (34 years old), a woman from Suzhou, and Gu Zhusheng (30 years old), a man from Nantong. They confiscated 780 forged lead 20-cent coins, 24 pieces of broken lead ingots used as raw materials, one steelyard, one iron ladle, one small silver coin, one wind furnace, and lead powder molds. They were taken to the police station. According to their confession, Bian Guiquan, who is at large, was in charge of the counterfeiting. The police chief ordered them to be detained. The next day, they were sent to the Second Special Court where Judge Zhang Chaozuo conducted the preliminary hearing. Attorney Yuan Jiahuan of the Police Department explained the case and requested an extension of the investigation to arrest the accomplices at large before initiating the trial. Detective Lü reported the arrest of the defendants and presented the seized evidence. Wang Ding confessed that Bian Ziquan proposed the counterfeiting and asked her to contribute 60 yuan as capital. Bian manufactured the coins, and they could make 20 to 30 coins per day. She and Gu are not a couple; Bian introduced Gu to her. Gu Zhusheng confessed that Bian Guiquan introduced him to Wang Ding. They could make 70 20-cent coins per day. After they were made, they were secretly sold for 1 yuan for every 15 lead coins. The court reviewed the confessions and ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody pending further hearing.

Kang Tih Road Vegetable Vendors Petition Chinese Directors Yesterday; Request Lu Bohong to Negotiate to Maintain Livelihoods

The vegetable stalls on Kang Tih Road in the French Concession were shut down by the French Concession Police. Fifty-one shops on Kang Tih Road jointly sent a letter to the French authorities requesting them to consider the livelihoods of the vendors and postpone the shutdown. However, it has been more than a month since the stalls were shut down, and there is no news of their resumption, which has left all the stallholders facing starvation. Therefore, they once again petitioned Chinese Director Lu Bohong yesterday morning. The details are recorded below:

Petition

Yesterday at around 5:00 AM, more than 110 stallholders, men, women, and children, gathered at Xieqiao in the Chinese Concession and walked to the Catholic Church in Dongjiadu, Xiaonanmen, to petition Lu Bohong, the Chinese Director of the French Municipal Council. When the vegetable vendors set off, they marched in orderly rows, carrying a large banner that read, "God bestows charity on the poor; requesting Mr. Lu Bohong to relieve the people's livelihood; a large petition from all the vegetable vendors on Kang Tih Road in the French Concession." They walked for about seven hours and arrived at the entrance of the Catholic Church, lining up on the road. The police on duty maintained order. Representatives of the stallholders, including Sun Chuanfu, delivered the petition to the church and requested to meet with Chinese Director Lu. Mr. Lu received them. At this time, the stallholders standing outside the door knelt down before Mr. Lu, appealing in unison. Mr. Lu persuaded the stallholders to stand up and promised to negotiate with the French Municipal Council immediately to find a way to resume the stalls. He also advised the vendors to return and wait patiently for a resolution. The vendors were satisfied and dispersed.

Petition Document

Respectfully presented, the vegetable vendors have been shut down from setting up stalls on Kang Tih Road by the French Concession Police for more than a month. Although they have shouted and appealed until their voices are hoarse, they have not received any indication from the authorities to resume the stalls, leaving hundreds of stallholders facing starvation. The vegetable vendors have previously detailed the situation and submitted a document to your esteemed Chinese Director, requesting your gracious relief. Now, because the livelihoods of the stallholders are in extreme danger and there is no way to maintain them, they are compelled to appeal to your esteemed position once again, requesting permission to make demands on the French Municipal Council to relieve the people's livelihood, without resorting to public disturbance, and so on.

Long-Distance Telephone Call Price Reduction at Night; Ministry of Communications Has Set New Measures; Effective December 1st

The Ministry of Communications has determined that the number of long-distance telephone calls at night is relatively low. It has now drafted measures to reduce the price of night calls. It stipulates that from 8:00 PM to 6:00 AM the next morning, the ordinary and urgent call charges will be calculated at 70% of the original price. The above measures are designated to be implemented in seven locations, including Beijing, Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Zhenjiang, from December 1st.

Yangtze River Had Two High Tides Yesterday; Low-Lying Roads Along the River Submerged by Three Inches; Dredging Bureau Predicts High Tides Again Today and Tomorrow

Yesterday, the Huangpu River experienced two high tides, both exceeding predictions. Low-lying areas along the river were submerged by three inches. According to a report from the Hydraulic Science Department of the Dredging Bureau, high tides will continue for the next two days. Details are recorded below:

Yangtze River Tide Rises to Shoreline

Yesterday, the weather was clear and the Yangtze River tide was still high, reaching the shoreline twice. The first time was at 0:27 AM, with a height of 11 feet 6.2 inches. The afternoon tide occurred at 0:49 PM, with a height of 11 feet 5 inches. At the intersection of Jiujiang Road and Sichuan Road, the roads near the East-West Continent Bank and the Four Banks Reserve were submerged by three inches. The roads between the banks on Jiujiang Road, including Datong, Sumitomo, Taiwan, Korea, Citibank, and Central, and from the Bund to Guangdong Road, were flooded. The roads in front of the Mobil Oil Company and Mitsubishi Bank at the intersection of Sichuan Road and Guangdong Road were also submerged by three inches. Cars splashed water as they drove past. The roads along the Bund at the Sixteenth Pier were also submerged by three inches, and water had reached the wharves. It is reported that the tide exceeded predictions, and the road flooding was caused by sewer backflow.

Continued High Tides Predicted for Today and Tomorrow

According to predictions from the Hydraulic Science Department of the Dredging Bureau, the Yangtze River will continue to experience high tides in the next two days. The times and heights are recorded below. The morning tide on the 14th will occur at 1:05 AM, with a height of 10 feet 0.9 inches. The afternoon tide will occur at 1:36 PM, with a height of 11 feet 2 inches. The morning tide on the 15th will occur at 1:53 AM, with a height of 10 feet 0.3 inches. The afternoon tide will occur at 2:20 PM, with a height of 11 feet.

Wuzhen Road Police Station Breaks Up Operation Specializing in Stealing Vehicle Parts; Four Male and Female Criminals Arrested; 175 Stolen Items Seized

Recently, incidents of rickshaws being robbed of their belongings have frequently occurred in Zhabei. The rickshaw pullers are mostly ignorant and uneducated people, so they dare not report to the police. The thieves therefore regard this as a business. After a rickshaw puller loses his belongings, the accomplices of the thieves would offer to help retrieve them, demanding a sum ranging from a few cents to several yuan. The rickshaw pullers often find that the money they earn from pulling the rickshaw for a day is not enough to redeem a lost item, which is truly infuriating. Luo Siwei, a police officer at the Wuzhen Road Police Station of the New Zha Sub-bureau, took pity on them. Therefore, he secretly dispatched patrol officers to investigate. At around 1:00 PM on the 11th of this month, Police Chief Hu Yao learned that a yellow rickshaw seat was found on the roof of a tin house behind the Xiaocai Market, and that the location was often used by accomplices of the thieves to negotiate the redemption of stolen goods. Unexpectedly, at 9:00 AM yesterday, Police Officer Zhao Huarong reported that stolen items specializing in yellow rickshaw parts were hidden in the stove shed at No. 11 Zhaohao Lane. Officer Luo immediately led Police Chief Hu Maokui and other officers to investigate. They found two oilcloth canopies, a quilt sewn from white cloth car covers (totaling twelve car covers), and one rickshaw puller's photo license number 25376. They also found twenty-nine car cushions and seventeen car covers in the loft, along with 115 oilcloth canopies. They arrested four male and female criminals: Jiang Hongmo, Wang Xiaomao, Wu Guanshi, and Huang. After interrogation, it was learned that Wu Guanshi was the cousin of Huang Yuxiang, the leader of the thieves. However, Huang had already fled. After verifying the confessions, Officer Luo immediately sent Jiang Hongmo, Wang Xiaomao, Wu Guanshi, and Huang, along with the stolen goods, including 117 oilcloth canopies and 29 car covers and cushions each, to the New Zha Sub-bureau for interrogation. It is reported that this location is a distribution point for stolen goods, and there is still a main location somewhere else.

Economic Pressure; Pitiful Suicide by Jumping from Building

Lu Changfang, 36 years old, from Haimen, Jiangbei, worked as a sales clerk in the building of the Western merchant Bi Liya Company at No. 25 French Avenue. He lived in the Bi Liya warehouse at No. 3 Lao Yong'an Street behind the building. Recently, due to economic pressure, he had a moment of despair. At 6:00 AM the day before yesterday, after getting up, Lu jumped from the window of the fifth floor of the warehouse, unnoticed. He fell to the ground, suffering severe head injuries and a broken right leg. His younger brother, Lu Weidian, and the head of the sales department, Wang Yiyin from Ningbo, discovered him, but it was too late. He died shortly after. They reported to the French police, who sent the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for an autopsy. An investigator investigated the cause of death. At noon that day, the Second Special Court was notified. Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with a forensic doctor and clerk, arrived at the funeral home. It was confirmed that the deceased Lu Changfang died from injuries sustained from jumping from the building while alive. The body was handed over to the family member, Lu Changxing Zhen, for funeral arrangements. The employer, a Westerner, sympathized with the poverty of the deceased's family and provided funds for the funeral and transportation back to his hometown for burial.

Yu Shunxing Accuses Adopted Son of Theft and Injuring His Parents; Court Orders Yu to Verify Injuries for Review

Yu Shunxing, 40 years old, a native of Cai residing at No. 24, Lane 10, Jia Siyi Road, French Concession, reported to the French Concession Police on the 8th of this month at 8:00 PM that his adopted son, Yu Jinfa, 24 years old, had committed theft and assault, injuring his parents. He requested arrest and prosecution. The police chief approved the request and ordered Detective Xu Daorong to arrest Yu Jinfa and send him to the Second Special Court for detention. The day before yesterday, Judge Zhang Chaozuo conducted a preliminary hearing in the First Criminal Court. Attorney Chen Ming of the Police Department explained the case. According to the accuser, the defendant was adopted as his son at the age of six and raised and trained to learn a trade to make a living. However, he did not engage in proper work. On June 14th of this year at 11:00 AM, he came to the house, stole clothes, and fled. On the 8th at 7:00 PM, he returned home and provoked a quarrel for no reason, injuring his head and face. He also constantly threatened to shoot him with a gun. Unable to bear the harassment, he had no choice but to report the arrest and request a heavy sentence. The defendant confessed, denying the theft and assault of his father. That night, he hit a cat, and his father was unhappy and falsely accused him of assaulting him. He reported the arrest and had him detained, requesting investigation. He did not commit the assault. The court reviewed the confessions and ordered a postponement of the hearing to the 21st. The defendant was remanded in custody, and the accuser was ordered to undergo a medical examination to verify the injuries for review by the court.

Qian Guojun; Gun Tied to Lower Leg

Yesterday at 5:30 PM, Liu Yunfang, the chief of the Yimiao Police Station, led police officers and Police Chief Wang Yuhai to inspect pedestrians in the area. While on Tudi Tang Street, they saw a person walking furtively. Seeing the police officers, he tried to avoid them. Chief Liu ordered him to stop and searched him. Nothing suspicious was found on his body. However, when they searched inside his socks, they found a six-inch Browning pistol tied to his lower leg (number 21807) and two bullets. When asked where the gun came from, he was evasive. He was immediately taken to the police station. It was found that the gun had been stolen from Xie Sanxin, a platoon leader of the Second Security Team, from his home. Xie is currently being held at the team headquarters. The defendant, Qian Guojun, 28 years old, from Suzhou, admitted to stealing the gun. When asked what he intended to use the gun for, he refused to answer. It was then discovered that the bullets were not original, indicating a possible robbery. In addition to a thorough interrogation, he will be sent to the General Bureau for trial.

Public Concession's Industrial Accident Report for September

According to the Public Works Department's report, a total of 198 industrial accidents occurred in factories in the Public Concession in September, including 8 deaths and 10 injured women. The causes of the accidents were largely clear in 176 cases, and known after investigation in 107 cases. In terms of industrial categories, the machinery and metal industry accounted for the largest number, with a total of 60 cases, including 2 deaths. In addition, there were 24 cases in the textile industry, 17 in the construction industry, 16 in the paper and printing industry, 15 in the tobacco and food industry, one death in the woodworking industry, one death in the clothing industry, and one death in the leather goods industry. In terms of the cause of the accidents, 51 people were injured by electrical machinery, including 3 deaths. Among these 51 people, 17 were injured by belts, pulleys, gears, etc., 3 were injured on elevators, 5 were injured by rollers, 4 were injured by pressure machines, and 5 were injured by rollers. There were 4 electrocution incidents, including one death. Ten people were burned by fire, including one death. Fourteen people were burned by hot objects or corrosives, including one death. Twenty-five people were injured by falling from heights, and 21 people were injured by falling objects. Fourteen people were injured by collisions. There were no deaths in the above cases. Seventeen people were injured in manual industries.

Stores on Rue de la Cité Road Request Expedited Pavement of Sidewalk

Due to the inconvenience of the paved cinder sidewalks after the reconstruction of the area, the stores on Rue de la Cité Road in the French Concession requested expedited pavement of the sidewalk. The stores on Rue de la Cité Road in the French Concession requested the Municipal Council of the Fourth District to negotiate because the road construction by the French Tramway Company, which began in April, had only been completed with paved cinders, which was still inconvenient. The council sent a letter to the French Municipal Council stating, "Respectfully, according to the stores on Rue de la Cité Road, the French Tramway Company has raised the road surface and rebuilt the road surface of Rue de la Cité Road, which took four months to complete. All the sidewalks along the road have also been raised with the road surface. Although the road construction has been completed, the sidewalks are still paved with cinders, which causes sand to blow into the stores on weekdays, and is inconvenient for pedestrians when it rains, which not only affects hygiene, but also impairs the view. It is requested that your council forward a letter to the French Municipal Council, ordering the Engineering Department to expedite the paving of cement on the sidewalks of both roads to benefit pedestrians and improve hygiene, etc. It is found that the stores on the two roads have suffered losses due to the inconvenience of transportation since the road construction began. Now that the road has been completed, the sidewalks should also be paved at the same time to benefit the businesses. It is requested that your council forward the letter to the Engineering Department to expedite the completion of the sidewalk paving on Rue de la Cité Road."

International and Domestic Female Telephone Operators Held Formal Examination Yesterday; Examination Site at Shanghai Elementary School; List of Accepted Names to Be Released in Three Days

Datong News Agency reports that the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications held a formal examination yesterday for international and domestic female telephone operators. Details are recorded below:

Number of Examinees

The Engineering Department of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau conducted preliminary reports and oral examinations at the bureau's exhibition room every morning since the 11th. As of noon the day before yesterday, the deadline, the number of applicants totaled more than 110. More than 60 people passed the oral examination and were issued examination certificates.

A Glimpse of the Examination Site

Yesterday at 9:00 AM, the formal examination was held at the Shanghai Elementary School on Qiaojia Road, Xiaonanmen. The examination site was on the upper and lower floors of the school building, divided into two classes. Many staff members from the Engineering Department were assigned to administer the examination.

Examination Items

The examinees brought their examination certificates and arrived at the site one after another, then entered the classrooms in classes and took their seats. The examiners distributed the questions and pencils and writing paper, and the examination began. The examination items in the morning were Chinese Language, Arithmetic, and World Geography. The examination items in the afternoon were Mandarin Chinese, English, Written Test, and Telephone Knowledge Interview.

Future Work

The names of those accepted will be released in three days. There will be 18 positions available. After receiving relevant training, these telephone operators will be prepared to be dispatched to the Zhabei long-distance exchange currently under construction.

Yu Qiaqing Telegraphed to Stop Xuchang Company from Purchasing Tobacco; Company Shareholders Also Issue Statement Acknowledging Company Is Now Under Foreign Control

The New Police News Agency reports that the Shanghai Tobacco Industry Association reported that the foreign British-American Tobacco Company was using Chinese nationals to establish the Xuchang Company in Xuchang, Henan, to monopolize tobacco leaves. The report was submitted to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, which petitioned the Ministry of Industry to investigate and stop the practice. This was reported in previous newspapers. Yu Qiaqing of the Ningbo Association telegraphed Chiang Kai-shek stating that this plan of the Xuchang Company affects the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people in the interior and requested that he preside over and stop it promptly. At the same time, Yang Peixiang, a shareholder and initiator of the Xuchang Company, also issued an important announcement (omitted) announcing that the company has now been taken over by foreign merchants. The details are recorded below:

Yu Qiaqing's Telegram

To Military Affairs Committee Chairman Chiang: The Xuchang area of Henan Province produces tobacco leaves. The tobacco industries of Beijing, Tianjin, Shanghai, and Hankou, and the cigarette manufacturers in various ports, all go there to purchase. No less than 300,000 Chinese people rely on this for a living. Most of the people engaged in this industry in Shanghai are from Ningbo. Several years ago, the foreign British-American Tobacco Company used a Chinese employee to set up a factory in Xuchang to purchase tobacco, smoke it, and sell it, controlling and oppressing the industry. This was discovered by the local authorities of the province, who immediately ordered it to stop, preserving the livelihoods of the Chinese people. Unexpectedly, someone is now colluding with foreign merchants and reviving the old trick. First, the Xuchang Company came forward to plan, and then the name of the Yu Su Baked Tobacco Factory was used to transfer it to the control of the foreign British-American Tobacco Company. Now, a huge sum of money has been raised to set up a factory there, and the weighing scale will be opened soon to purchase tobacco, with the intention of making a clean sweep. The industry is calling on all parties to work together to stop this foreign economic invasion, which, if implemented, will cut off the livelihoods of the Chinese people. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has also verified the facts and sent separate telegrams to request intervention. However, it has recently been heard that those colluding with foreign merchants dare to use the name of the Tobacco Leaf Improvement Committee to achieve their private goals. Because this matter concerns the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people, I dare not withhold what I have heard. Therefore, I telegraph to you, Your Excellency, requesting you to preside over and telegraph to the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Henan Provincial Government to forcefully stop it, so as to avoid harming the locality and maintain the people's livelihoods. The fellow villagers are deeply grateful and send their best wishes. Your younger brother Yu HeDe respectfully bows. Issued by the Ningbo Association in Shanghai.

Central News Agency reports that the Oriental Industrial Conference has been scheduled to be held in Shanghai on the 18th. Baron Iba Kwasaburo, the leader of the Japanese delegation attending the conference, and others are scheduled to depart from Tokyo on the 14th and arrive in Shanghai on the 17th to attend. Iba is scheduled to leave Shanghai on the 21st for Beijing, arrive in Tianjin on the 23rd, and arrive in Beiping on the 25th to investigate the economic and industrial conditions in various parts of China before going to Dalian and returning to Japan via the Northeast.

British Merchant Establishes Lun Chang Company in Pudong; Dividing Into Spinning, Weaving, Bleaching, Dyeing, and Printing Departments with New Equipment

The factory established by the British Lun Chang Textile Bleaching Dyeing and Printing Co., Ltd. in Pudong is grand in scale and has long been completed. Its machines are all the latest British models and are divided into spinning, weaving, bleaching, dyeing, and printing departments. Senior management personnel, such as technicians, are all British, but the workers are all Chinese. It has been in operation for a long time. Last month, a female worker in the weaving department had a conflict with the British manager, causing a strike. It was resolved after persuasion by Director Zhang of the Pudong Branch of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau. It is said that this is the first time that British merchants have established a bleaching and printing factory in Shanghai.

After the Italian-Ethiopian War, Chinese Merchants Purchased a Large Amount of Pigments, Totalling Over Two Million Yuan in Chinese Currency. The Association Resolved That All Goods Must Be Paid for in Cash.

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, Shanghai’s Western pigment merchants and various regional associations in Shanghai, recalling the European War of 1914, when pigment imports were cut off, prices soared more than tenfold, and profits were substantial, have recently been closely monitoring the Italian-Ethiopian War. With the League of Nations passing sanctions, fearing a similar event to 1914, they have been actively contacting German and other foreign firms to purchase large amounts of spot goods, amounting to over two million yuan in Chinese currency. The German firm's pigment inventory in its warehouses has been completely cleared, an unprecedented event. Subsequently, the Shanghai Western Pigment Industry Association specifically resolved that no pre-orders would be accepted, and all sales would be for cash. Their announcement is recorded as follows: The association's merchants are concerned that sales to customers may fluctuate, leading to disputes during account settlement. For the sake of the industry's business interests, rectification is required. At the 21st standing committee meeting on the 7th of this month, it was resolved that since the start of the Italian-Ethiopian War, foreign firms are not accepting pre-orders for sales, and payment in cash is required upon completion of the transaction. As the firms are now implementing this method, all merchants should follow suit and not accept pre-orders, with all sales being for cash. This has been passed and recorded. In addition to sending separate notifications, this announcement is hereby issued, urging all merchants to comply accordingly. This notice.

Jue Yuan to Hold a Ceremony for the Presentation of a Bodhi Tree, and the Library Will Open Simultaneously on a Set Date.

Indian monk Lade, during his visit to China, brought a branch of a "Bodhi Tree" from India. According to Buddhist tradition, Siddhartha Gautama attained enlightenment under this tree, hence its name, making it exceptionally precious. Monk Lade has specially presented this branch to the owner of Jue Yuan in Shanghai for planting. The garden will hold a presentation ceremony on the 19th of this month, inside the garden on Avenue Haig, and has invited Madam Hardoon to unveil it. Simultaneously, the library will hold its opening ceremony at 2:00 PM. The library has been in preparation for years by Chairman Ye Yuhu, Director Guan Jiongzhi, Wang Yiting, and others, and is now ready. The library's collection includes major Buddhist scriptures and legal codes from the Tang and Song dynasties, as well as valuable scriptures from England, France, and India, all meticulously collected. After the opening, it will be open year-round for public reading. Additionally, a Dharma Treasure Hall is actively being planned. This hall will display collections of Buddhist images, Dharma treasures, and ritual implements from home and abroad throughout history. Currently, Mr. Ye has personally donated 10,000 yuan for preparatory expenses. On the 19th, Shanghai Buddhist community will unite with Jue Yuan to bid farewell to Monk Lade. At that time, Ye Yuhu, Wang Yiting, Guan Jiongzhi, Qu Yingguang, Master Taixu, Master Dabei, and others will attend and deliver speeches.

Inventor Yang Ming Invents a Method for Manufacturing Artificial White Sugar and Has Applied to the Academia Sinica for Support.

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, Mr. Yang Ming, who last year invented methods for making artificial vegetables, artificial flowers, and artificial kerosene, has not only had his inventions published in newspapers and displayed at the Chamber of Commerce for testing but has also invited social leaders to organize the China Kerosene Company to produce "Elephant Brand" kerosene in China for the benefit of the national economy and the people's livelihood. Mr. Yang, based on recent customs statistics that show the annual value of sugar imports to be 135 million yuan, believes that if no immediate remedy is sought, the leakage is unimaginable. He plans to manufacture artificial white sugar using vegetable protein (the fibrous substance of beets and sugarcane, derived from the artificial vegetable method), flour (a component that helps create the sweet substance in beets, and a similar element to the white powder in sugarcane), and iron oxide (the outer coating of sugarcane, which combines to form the sweet elements of white sugar after sugarcane develops) as the basic raw materials. He intends to invent a method for making artificial white sugar in the near future to supplement the insufficient supply of planted beets and sugarcane. However, due to limited financial resources, he intends to gather comrades to promote the project together and has applied to the Academia Sinica for support.

The Leven Case Will Be Heard Tomorrow.

Mr. He Fu, the liquidator of three companies including the American-Oriental Bank, previously filed three civil lawsuits against Mr. Leven in the U.S. Court for China, requesting the court to order Mr. Leven to return the remuneration of 135,000 taels each, along with three years' interest, that he illegally received in 1932 from the American-Oriental Bank, the American Eastern Banking Corporation, and the Probstfield Estate Company. He also filed a criminal lawsuit, alleging that Mr. Leven, along with Mr. Triscott, the manager of the American Eastern Banking Corporation, and Mr. Blanc, the accountant of the company, had misused securities entrusted to them by clients. The first of the civil cases is now scheduled to be heard by Chief Judge Helmick of the U.S. Court at 10:00 AM on Tuesday, the 15th of this week. Mr. Evans, Mr. Leven's lawyer, has arrived in Shanghai from Tianjin to handle the case. Dr. Slater is Mr. He Fu's lawyer, and it is expected that many will attend the hearing that day. The criminal case is scheduled to be heard on October 29th, by which time the first civil case should have concluded. Mr. He Fu has also requested the court to recover the overdraft and unpaid promissory notes owed by Mr. Leven to the American-Oriental Bank, and the amount owed by Mr. Leven to the American Eastern Banking Corporation is even larger. This debt will be heard after the criminal case concludes.

Xinji Bank Extends Time for Clearing Small Deposits

According to the Zi Lin Bao, staff at the Xinji Bank at 100 Jiujiang Road stated that the bank recently decided to start repaying deposits of less than 50 yuan last Friday. The bank's office hours are from 9:00 AM to noon and from 2:00 PM to 6:00 PM, with the first day ending at 5:00 PM. A total of 201 depositors withdrew 4,336.50 yuan. The total payout for the two days was 5,468.17 yuan. There are a total of 628 small depositors, with total deposits reaching nearly 10,000 yuan. As depositors are slow to withdraw, the clearing of small deposits has to be extended.

Fire at Xie Hengxing in Yimiao

Xie Hengxing store with a shop at No. 4 Yimiao Road in the city suddenly caught fire at 1:00 AM yesterday. Flames shot out in all directions. The 25th patrolman at the location, Shang Xinwen, upon hearing the alarm, immediately reported it to the station and relayed it to the fire brigade. Fire trucks from various districts arrived at the scene and made every effort to extinguish the fire. Since the Central District Fire Brigade was nearby, it was able to put out the fire, preventing a major disaster. Only the goods inside the store were damaged. After investigation, it was found that the store was not insured. The fire starter, Xie Yongfu, was taken to the station and confessed that the fire was caused by carelessness, disrupting order. He was sent to the bureau for interrogation.

The Dongfang Steel Fine Factory, located at 750 Kunming Road, had previously declared closure due to financial difficulties. Even the rent was four months in arrears. The landlord filed a lawsuit with the U.S. Consular Court, which ruled that all the factory's assets be auctioned off to cover the debt. However, the workers also had unpaid wages. Yesterday at around 8:00 PM, two former factory workers, Chen Axiang, also known as Dang Shuren, 49 years old, and Wu Xianwen, from Changzhou, 30 years old, claimed that the factory still owed them around 150 yuan in wages each and had not received any news of payment for a long time. They went with their wives, Zhou, 28 years old, and Xu, 27 years old, to demand payment. However, they were stopped by the factory's gatekeeper, Zhang Xiuzhang, from Shandong, 20 years old. This led to a verbal argument, and neither side would give way, eventually resulting in a physical altercation. Zhang Xiuzhang was outnumbered and beaten by the two couples. Nearby patrolmen noticed and rushed to intervene, finding Zhang Xiuzhang spitting blood and clutching his chest in pain. They quickly sent him to the hospital for treatment and took the assailants to the police station for further investigation.

Negotiation Regarding the Capsizing of the Xiexing Tugboat

The Xieshun tugboat of the Xiexing Shipping Company, at around 4:00 PM on the 8th of this month in Yangjia Du, Pudong, was towing two barges filled with flower clothes owned by Chen Maolang and Shen A-huo into the Suzhou River (commonly known as the Old Port), intending to turn from the middle of the Huangpu River to enter the port. However, the tugboat driver, while approaching Puxi to enter the port, due to the rapid tide, was unable to support one of the flower clothes barges being towed at the rear, which immediately capsized. All the people on the boat fell into the water and were rescued, but the flower clothes were all lost. Besides those recovered, five pieces are still missing, along with various equipment from the boat. The various expenses including salvage costs are estimated to be around 5-6,000 yuan. Currently, the barge owners are in negotiations with the Xiexing Company, demanding compensation, but no satisfactory resolution has been reached. They have filed a lawsuit in court to seek recovery.

Mixing Counterfeit Banknotes Awaiting Sentencing

Lin Degen from Haizhou, on the morning of the 2nd of this month at 9:00 AM, snuck into the cigarette and paper shop of Xiao Guangrong, a man from Shandong, at No. 3, Lane 922, East Broadway Road, mixing a counterfeit one-yuan banknote from the China and South Bank. The case was discovered and he was arrested by Chinese detective Yin Zhanqing. Two counterfeit one-yuan banknotes from the China and South Bank and one counterfeit ten-yuan banknote from China were found in his sleeve. He was taken to the Huishan police station and confessed that the counterfeit banknotes belonged to Mr. Hu Wang, who lived on Beijing Jiang Road, Zhabei. The Public Security Bureau subsequently arrested Mr. Hu Wang and brought him back to the police station. They were separately sent to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday, Judge Jiang Shuzi of the Third Criminal Court conducted the trial. The Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer, Li Zhishan, presented the case and requested punishment according to the law. When questioned, Lin Degen insisted that on the morning of his arrest, at around 7:00 AM, he went to Mr. Hu Wang's house, who gave him the three counterfeit banknotes. If he spent ten yuan, he would be paid two yuan, and one yuan would be exchanged for two jiao. When questioned, Mr. Hu Wang claimed that around November of last year, his mistress borrowed ten yuan in Yuan Shikai silver dollars from him. He couldn't get it back, and he argued and fought with his son, leading to resentment and false accusations. He also hired a miscellaneous lawyer to defend him. Lin Degen denied borrowing money and fighting, and Mr. Hu Wang denied having a mistress. Judge Jiang ordered them to be remanded in custody separately, awaiting sentencing.

Notice from the Pilotage Administration Committee Regarding Scheduled Assessments

The Shanghai Pilotage Administration Committee issued Notice No. 8 yesterday, stating that a final assessment for short-term Chinese pilots in the Songhu District is scheduled to be conducted by the committee. The assessment will begin on October 1st of this year. All Chinese pilots who currently hold pilot licenses issued by the Ministry of the Navy (which are now invalid), or who previously held such licenses and have had them revoked, those who have not reported for assessment without a license, or those who have previously been assessed but failed, are eligible to participate in this assessment. They must report to the Songhu District Pilotage Office by October 30th. Those holding licenses from the Ministry of the Navy must also present and surrender them at the same time, without delay. Those who are eligible for the issuance of pensions according to regulations may be approved for pensions and do not need to participate in the assessment. The specific assessment methods and regulations for qualifying as a pilot or receiving a pension will be separately notified to all relevant parties by the committee on October 28th. This notice is hereby issued.

The Gong Wu Stage Performs the Famous Play "Yang Jiao Yuan"

Since hiring the famous Jing Chao opera star Li Wanchun, the Gong Wu Stage in Shanghai has been selling out every day. Li Wanchun has also rehearsed "Yang Jiao Yuan". The play is based on the "Ancient and Modern Wonders" and portrays the life-and-death friendship between Yang Jiao'ai and Zuo Botao, serving as a sharp critique of current society. The play was once performed by a famous opera troupe in Beijing during the early Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty, under the name "Alliance of Loyalty". Afterwards, it almost disappeared. Li Wanchun has a secret copy of the play, which has been revised several times by writers and playwrights to become a unique masterpiece. Li plays Yang Jiao'ai in the play, and his performance of the plum blossom double swords in the oath-taking scene is particularly brilliant. Xiaokuiguan plays Zuo Botao, and Mao Qinglai plays Gao Jianli, their passionate and tragic performances are enough to uplift the spirit.

Letter to the Editor

To the Editor, I recently read an article in today's newspaper about the opening of the Shanghai World Amusement Park, which stated that the park was established to provide relief for flood victims and quoted me as reporting on the preparations. This does not correspond with the facts. The park was established by Mr. Hu, Mr. Shen, and others with invested funds and is purely a commercial organization, distinct from the previous flood relief amusement fair. Whether or not a portion of the profits will be donated to flood relief is not something I can speculate on, as I am not a member of the organization. I only attended the park yesterday as a guest and offered a few words of congratulation. There was no mention of the so-called preparatory process. Fearing future misunderstandings, I hereby send this letter to be published in your column as a statement. Sincerely, Cao Gong, October 13th.
