Discussion

Massacre in East Africa

— Xing An

The East African war has already broken out. Italy declared war without warning on the third day, sending its army and air force to launch a fierce offensive from the north, east, and south, carrying out a massive slaughter. The Italo-Ethiopian incident, which had been in stalemate for ten months, has now seen Italy hurl its first bomb at Ethiopia, stirring up the atmosphere worldwide. Mussolini's ambition is fully exposed here. After the two armies made contact, Ethiopia immediately filed a protest with the League of Nations, and Italy also notified the League of Nations of its actions. The Palace of Peace in Geneva will inevitably be destroyed again soon.

Although the Italo-Ethiopian conflict has only been underway for ten days, the fighting is extremely fierce, with heavy losses on both sides. It is reported that the Italian army in Madahar, led by Mussolini's two sons and one son-in-law, launched a heavy bombing raid on Aduwa on the third day. Approximately two thousand women, children, and soldiers were killed or injured, a very tragic scene. Ciano also destroyed the royal palace of Aduwa, making a great contribution. Mussolini should be proud to have such a brave son-in-law.

In this Italian military campaign, an Ethiopian Askari army of black soldiers has joined the fighting. These black soldiers are like walking powder kegs, carrying weapons such as machine guns, pistols, handguns, and broadswords. When they entered Ethiopian territory, they sang loudly in their local language, vowing to cut off the Ethiopian Emperor's beard and make it into a small brush to shine Mussolini's boots. Some people who see this may not be able to help but scold the Askari people for being shameless. I think it is unnecessary. These black people originally had no intention of killing their own kind. They were probably coerced for a time. When the Ethiopian Emperor's beard is indeed cut off and made into a small brush, they will realize that they are just slaves, only fit to shine Mussolini's boots, and it will be too late to regret.

Who will win the Italo-Ethiopian war in the future? This is difficult to predict. In terms of strength, Ethiopia is certainly no match for Italy. In terms of popular sentiment, the entire Ethiopian nation is united in hatred of the enemy and has made the determination to resist the enemy to the death, which cannot be taken lightly. However, the Italo-Ethiopian war is not limited to one corner of East Africa. Looking at Britain's recent actions, it seems intent on imposing sanctions on Italy. On the other hand, Italy has already stated that anyone who dares to impose sanctions will be met with war. It can be seen that it is possible for the Italo-Ethiopian conflict to trigger a war between Britain and Italy. Not only that, but a spark can start a prairie fire. It is possible that it will expand into a second world war. Today's Italo-Ethiopian war may be the prelude to the next world war.

The Peddler

— Green Leaf

—Impressions of an Ancient City—

What stands out in the ancient city is the peddler selling groceries. Usually, the peddler only sells some needles, threads, head ropes, wooden combs, buttons, and some small items for women. Sometimes he also sells photos of the Shanghai cityscape, but that is rare. The peddler carries a small rattle drum in his hand, carries a glass cabinet on his back, and walks around the streets and alleys, with the small rattle drum ringing everywhere. In the afternoon, the yellow sunlight pants on the roofs of the black houses. While the entire ancient city is lonely, the peddler's small rattle drum rings "de long long long long" in the hazy space for most of the day. There is no poetic rhythm, but it sounds light and comfortable. Standing in the building at this time, you can see the tattered hat moving in the air, moving, coming in from the hutong mouth, moving step by step, stopping at the door of the tailor shop next door. The small rattle drum is still ringing "de long long long long." Now you can see clearly that under the tattered hat, there is a smile formed out of habit, a flat, knowing face, and the eyes are thrown on the women on the road and the women who patronize him diligently.

At this time, the children who like to join in the fun often drag their parents to the peddler to ask for one or two Shanghai street scene photos. This item is very good for the peddler's business. A hundred photos can be sold out in four or five days, but the peddlers sell this item very rarely. Ask ten peddlers, and only two or three sell this photo, and no one can ask a definite reason.

When women lack small items such as needles and threads, they find the peddler selling groceries. They want this and that around the glass cabinet, like turning over the baskets in the field, just making a noisy sound. So the peddler takes out the items one by one from the glass cabinet, piling them up in a mess, always saying the same set of words: "Take your time, take your time! Everyone has it!" As he says this, he points to the items. The peddler is also a very capable small businessman. He knows who wants what and gives them what they want. In a few minutes, everything is done, and the customers pay and take the items. If they don't have change with them, they can also buy on credit and pay a few days later. Every peddler knows how to do business and is sensible. He greets and asks people he doesn't know.

The small tailor shop also asks the peddler for a few buttons and threads and other items each time, and the tailor shop has an account; the account is settled and paid off at the end of the year, and not a penny is missing, and the transaction is fair. This is probably due to the simplicity and honesty of the people of the ancient city.

When everything is done well and the transaction is settled, the peddler carries the glass cabinet on his back, shakes the small rattle drum, and leaves the hutong. In the distance, I can also hear the small drum sound, "de long long long long," just ringing lonely in the dust, in the ancient city.

Looking at the peddler's small rattle drum, I often think of the peddler in my hometown. The peddler in my hometown is also exactly the same as the peddler in this ancient city, only a few minor differences. The peddler in my hometown also carries a small rattle drum in his hand and carries a glass cabinet on his back, selling some needles, threads, head ropes, and small items for women. The difference is that he doesn't go to the city to sell them. The market in our city is prosperous, so the peddler only walks around the villages and towns, taking the small rattle drum and running on the village roads. If you prick up your ears, you can also vaguely hear the "de long long long long" drum sound ringing in the distance.

And the market in this ancient city is not as good as ours. Loneliness and desolation are the true colors of the ancient city. Therefore, the peddler can transport some things from other places and sell them in the city, but he does not go to the countryside. This is also a kind of deformed development in the ancient city.

The Story of Cutting Off the Queue

— Tian

The winding, towering mountain city firmly locks the thoughts of the people in Village A and Village B, who seem never to interact with each other, and cuts off the line of sight of those who are not allowed to look at the vast world. Mountains, water, green mountains, and green water are the materials we villagers discuss and the world we display.

When I was only five years old, I was studying in a private school. In the early morning, when we had not yet finished our morning class, the nearsighted, shoe-brush-bearded Mr. Li suddenly adopted a reserved tone, as if he understood the trends of the outside world, and said:

"Now the emperor... is gone, is... gone, um! It's over! It's over!... I heard that we have to cut off our queues, we have to cut off our queues! But, this is actually a... good thing! The queue is annoying!"

As he said this, he scratched at the root of his queue, and the fingernails, about four inches long, on his right hand picked at the black dirt under the fingernails of his left hand, and he took out a black grain and put it on the table. He smelled it with his nose and eyes for a while, pressed his thumb on the table, and a small spitting sound came out. Although the spitting sound was drowned out by the sound of reading, the older children all knew it was a louse. They did not dare to laugh out loud, and those closer to the teacher would put their books up to cover their laughing faces. Those who were more advanced would pretend to ask him to tell them what the book was about, and would tell him in passing. Those who were equal would cough and pull their mouths at the teacher. In less than a quarter of an hour, everyone in the class of more than ten people knew about it. I thought that "the young ones are mischievous," and I already knew about this matter. So I joined them in a burst of laughter, laughing so hard that my nose became a big bunch of drums. At this time, the teacher was pacing back and forth, as if proud of his knowledge of current affairs. As soon as he walked in front of me and heard my laughter, he rewarded me with a nail-like cane. My laughter had not yet stopped, and I immediately turned around and cried.

I cried sadly, as if I had suffered a great injustice.

The students snickered, and the sound was obviously not something that reading could cover up.

"Now!" The teacher walked to his seat and clapped the gavel.

He shook the queue behind him, which was as thin as a cigarette butt, "Cutting it off is a good thing, but without the emperor, without the emperor... it's over, it's over!"

After the morning class was dismissed, we walked out of the school gate. The school was located in an ancient temple on the highest mountain peak. Standing in front of the temple, we could look out over the mountains and into the distance, where the mist spread over the vast sea of smoke.

"That's where the rebellion is taking place; it's over there!"

Although children's hearts have the light of the future, their vision is small—and it is also locked in the mountains. Outside the mountains is like a foreign country, it is the place of rebellion.

When I returned home, I had a small bump on my forehead, as big as a hill. My mother asked me with concern, with a sympathetic eye and a loving attitude, which fueled my arrogance, and I cried and cried.

"What are you crying for!—You didn't study hard, so the teacher beat you?"

My father had just returned from the farm. He had never been very polite to me. As he said this, he glared at me. This glare frightened me so much that even my tearless cry brought out tears.

My mother represented the story once, and my father's attention was not on the problem of hitting me, but on the problem of cutting off the queue. He said:

"First cut off my queue, then I have to comb it, and it takes more oil. It's more convenient to cut it off!" To say something fashionable now, my father was like a "progressive figure," although his starting point was utilitarianism.

"You want to be a monk?—I don't want to be a monk's wife," my mother put me on her body, "and you don't want to be a monk's son," my mother used the means of threatening capitalists with a general strike to deal with my father.

"You'll be a nun, and he'll be a little monk." My father followed with a big laugh.

However, don't look down on that Mr. Li. He had quite a bit of magic. This news was probably spread to the homes by the students, and then spread out. The whole village was a sensation: the teacher was a person who "reads the books of sages," and what he said always had a basis.

Several rash young men, you secretly cut mine, and I will retaliate against you. Before long, there were more people with disheveled hair, but when they met, they would call each other "screech owl, exposing the ugliness of his grandmother's house." This was the attitude of the old women, and the young women would laugh and pray to heaven and earth when they saw someone cut off their queue.

Later, it turned into a trend. But the old people didn't cut off their queues so rashly. I remember the day my father "lowered his hair." He lit a lamp and burned incense in front of the ancestral tablet, and added four bows and eight prostrations. My mother also could not resist the impact of that trend, and she herself wielded the knife. With one snip, my father's queue and head separated. My father respectfully placed it on the incense burner. What for? I'm afraid he couldn't answer it either, while only a "chamber pot lid" remained on my head, so I avoided the disaster of a knife.

—It's the Republic of China now, and the Republic of China doesn't want queues anymore.

Later, this news finally got through to the mountain city, and our Mr. Li was only left with a bald tail.

It has been twenty-four years since the queue was cut!

Recent Works by Mr. Chen Weikuan of Chaoyang

Page 24

Entertainment

— Yan

Today, Master Zhu's house is hosting a grand banquet, a miracle unseen in this town since time immemorial. Although Master Zhu is the wealthiest man in town, he only associates with people of high standing. But their comings and goings are always clandestine, as if they were committing a crime. He always uses the side gate, and those distinguished guests are also willing to enter and exit through the side gate. Except for the first and fifteenth of each month, when Master Zhu sits in his blue sedan chair to offer incense at the City God Temple, the two black lacquered doors are only briefly opened and closed when the chair enters and exits. This is because Master Zhu once held some official position. A gentleman does not forget his past, and the City God blessed him with so much wealth, so he cannot forget offering incense on the first and fifteenth of each month. Moreover, he must be respectful and reverent, entering and exiting through the main gate, so that this fortunate relic – the blue sedan chair – does not become a haven for silverfish.

Many of the farmers in the surrounding areas are Master Zhu's tenants. Every year, they have to go to the granary (Note 1) to pay rent. Some want to take this opportunity to inquire about the secrets within the two black lacquered doors, but Master Zhu himself uses the side gate, and the tenants can only enter and exit through the back door. Master Zhu's residence, known throughout the town as the "ten mansions with nine courtyards" (Note 2), has the accounting office located in the last mansion. What the tenants see is the back gate of a garden, secured with a foot-long iron lock. There is also a row of five large granaries, with piles of rice stalks as high as the roof ridge; and, of course, the account's face as stern as the City God. (To be continued)

A Bundle of Radio Waves

Generals Tong Lei and Ruan Jiao, your pens are "indeed" good, your art of scolding people is "not bad" either, but I think you two are "eating your own food and meddling in other people's business", which is probably not worth it, right? In my opinion, you two don't need to shout like Zhang Fei: "Who dares to fight me a hundred rounds," and you don't need to say vulgarities like "illegitimate child". Everyone is "looking for hairs in an egg, seeking silk on ivory chopsticks". In the end, the hatred will only deepen. If you attack me and I attack you, won't there be one more enemy in the broadcasting world in the future? As the saying goes, "When two tigers fight, one must be injured." If one is injured, will the other gain a few pieces of meat? Good! Let me think of a "diplomatic solution"! It is said, "No fight, no friendship." The ancients have proven this to us. Although you two are not really fighting, it is almost the same. Well, I won't talk anymore. I trust that the two generals will understand. Otherwise, I will have to ask the two generals to follow Zeng Shen of Bei and "think thrice before acting"! (Ugly Woman)

The battle of words between the two esteemed brothers, Ruan Jiao and Tong Lei, is truly fought with real swords and spears, and has gone on for several rounds. In fact, you two are too competitive. Brother Tong Lei is too full to do anything, and insists on looking for trouble. Brother Ruan Jiao also refuses to admit his mistakes. So you fire a gun, he swings a knife, and the great battle begins. It is said that Brother Ruan Jiao is a poor young scholar who makes a living by writing articles for稿費. He is still editing publications now, so I think he would certainly be willing to give in. I also heard that Brother Tong Lei is the young owner of ×× Cafe at No. 48, Penglai Market. Fortunately, he has food and shelter, so he can afford to meddle in other people's business. Brother Jiao, Brother Lei, do you agree? (Iron Pen)

Since there is a peacemaker coming forward in the battle between Tong Lei and Ruan Jiao, I think both sides should rest. The facts will eventually prove it to you. (Editor)

Dear Editor: After reading Mr. Ji Hongshou's letter in the Radio column of your esteemed newspaper on the 12th, regarding the Mei華 Music Association, I am extremely surprised. Our association was established in the spring of 1931 and has a history of three years. At that time, we broadcast on radio stations such as Da Zhonghua, Yuanchang, Foyin, Zhongxi, Anding, and Huadong, with evidence from the directors of each radio station. Moreover, our association members are currently broadcasting in various broadcasting organizations in Shanghai. Those who hold the position of president include the presidents of Man Society, Egret Society, Lao Yanyan Society, Jue Shi Harmonica Society, Hao Hao Society, and Rose Society, all of whom are members of our association. From this, it can be seen that our association has a long history, strong strength, and abundant talent. There is no need to boast, as the facts speak for themselves. The Meihua Music Association led by Mr. Li has only recently emerged and suddenly wants to usurp our association's name. Who is right and wrong, who came first and who came later, the facts will prove. It cannot be distinguished by empty words. Therefore, please ask Mr. Li to inquire at major radio stations and organizations in Shanghai, and he will know the history and reality of our association. Also, please change the word "Meihua" of the association as soon as possible to clarify the situation and avoid misunderstanding by various sectors. Enclosed is a news item about our association from the Radio Weekly of April 13, 1934. (Omitted) Old-Brand Meihua Music Association Leaders Ma Tinglong and Liu Mohong, respectfully, October 12th.

Movie News

Introduction to "Jade Horse"

"Jade Horse" is Xu Xinfu's great work after "Street Willow Wall Flower." Viewers probably haven't forgotten the touching aspects of "Street Willow Wall Flower". The personalities of each of its leading actors are portrayed so vividly that even every small movement is extremely typical. In "Jade Horse," directed by Xu Jun this time, he further demonstrates his inherent strengths. Wang Zhengxin in "Jade Horse" plays a resolute and unyielding detective. When Zhao Dan, the president of the Anti-Drug Association, is assassinated, he runs around all night, trying to solve the case. In the apartment of the socialite Yan Yuexian, he unintentionally discovers something related to the Zhao Dan case. He uses this to track down the residence of Gong Jianong, who sells poison pills. Sure enough, at Gong Jianong's residence, he finds a zinc plate with a poisonous substance trademark. This further confirms his involvement in the murder of Zhao Dan. He then tries every means to solve the case. As a result, Gong Jianong finally admits that he is a drug dealer and is captured by him.

The socialite Yan Yuexian loves Zhao Dan, but Zhao Dan does not love her. Gong Jianong, on the other hand, is the most ardent pursuer of her. Later, when Gong Jianong and Wang Zhengxin have a conflict at her home, she is killed by stray bullets. Gong Jianong is a villain who sells poison pills, leading many of his henchmen to transport large quantities of poison pills from this city to another city. His methods are extremely ruthless. When he learns that Zhao Dan is working hard to promote the anti-drug movement, he resolutely beats him to death. Later, when he knows that Wang Zhengxin has discovered his secret, he goes to assassinate Wang Zhengxin. After much torment, he is finally arrested. Next to be mentioned is Gu Lanjun. She is an innocent woman. Because of her youth, she only knows how to seek pleasure every day. Like other young ladies of the bourgeoisie, she goes in and out of dance halls and bars every day. She is a good friend of the villain Gong Jianong, but she doesn't know his secrets at all. … The characters in "Jade Horse" are all vivid and have very distinct personalities, such as Wang Zhengxin's resourcefulness, Yan Yuexian's romanticism, Gong Jianong's ruthlessness, and Gu Lanjun's innocence and dissipation. They can all be seen in their every move.

"Jade Horse," the first Chinese sound detective film, is indeed novel and exciting. It is expected that it will cause a sensation when it is released.

Star Film Company is scheduled to hold a "Star Singing Night" at the city center stadium tonight (the 14th) to welcome athletes from the National Games. This is Miss Hu Die's pose when singing.

"Hero of the Times" Unofficial History

— Bai Mu

Is it "heroes who create the times" or "the times that create heroes"? The upcoming Yihua sound film "Hero of the Times" will tell you clearly.

"Hero of the Times" is a history of social changes in China over the past fifty years.

"Hero of the Times" features the appearance, activities, rise, and fall of different characters from all walks of life in current society.

Ying Yunwei has the ambition to show "Hero of the Times" to friends who usually welcome foreign films.

"Hero of the Times," whether in terms of directing techniques, photography skills, actor acting, or even recording, set design, and other aspects, can rival foreign films.

Shang Guanwu is the "hero" in "Hero of the Times," and Hu Ping is the "beauty."

"Hero of the Times" has realistic themes, profound descriptions, and even sharp and acute dissections.

"Hero of the Times" is the most glorious structure in the history of Chinese cinema.

"Hero of the Times" is an honorary production of Yihua Company, who spared no expense and exhausted a lot of money to complete the raising of Chinese film standards.

Zhou Ke has made a contribution to the new photography techniques in "Hero of the Times."
